line 1:     " Build up a map command like

line 3:     let plug = '<Plug>NERDCommenter' . a:target
line 4:     let plug_start = 'noremap <silent> ' . plug . ' :call nerdcommenter#Comment("'
line 5:     let plug_end = '", "' . a:target . '")<CR>'
line 6:     " Build up a menu command like
line 7:     " 'menu <silent> comment.Comment<Tab>\\cc <Plug>NERDCommenterComment'
line 8:     let menuRoot = get(['', 'comment', '&comment', '&Plugin.&comment', '&Plugin.Nerd\ &Commenter'], g:NERDMenuMode, '')
line 10:     let menu_command = 'menu <silent> ' . menuRoot . '.' . escape(a:desc, ' ')
line 11:     if strlen(a:combo)
line 12:         let leader = exists('g:mapleader') ? g:mapleader : '\'
line 13:         let menu_command .= '<Tab>' . escape(leader, '\') . a:combo
line 14:     endif
line 15:     let menu_command .= ' ' . (strlen(a:combo) ? plug : a:target)
line 16:     " Execute the commands built above for each requested mode.
line 17:     for mode in (a:modes ==# '') ? [''] : split(a:modes, '\zs')
line 18:         if strlen(a:combo)
line 19:             execute mode . plug_start . mode . plug_end
line 19: nnoremap <silent> <Plug>NERDCommenterComment :call nerdcommenter#Comment("n", "Comment")<CR>
line 20:             if g:NERDCreateDefaultMappings && !hasmapto(plug, mode)
line 21:                 execute mode . 'map <leader>' . a:combo . ' ' . plug
line 21: nmap <leader>cc <Plug>NERDCommenterComment
line 22:             endif
line 23:         endif
line 24:         " Check if the user wants the menu to be displayed.
line 25:         if g:NERDMenuMode !=# 0

line 168: " Returns the git-diff hunks for the file or an empty list if there
line 169: " aren't any hunks.
line 170: "
line 171: " The return value is a list of lists.  There is one inner list per hunk.
line 172: "
line 173: "   [
line 174: "     [from_line, from_count, to_line, to_count],
line 175: "     [from_line, from_count, to_line, to_count],
line 176: "     ...
line 177: "   ]
line 178: "
line 179: " where:
line 180: "
line 181: " `from`  - refers to the staged file
line 182: " `to`    - refers to the working tree's file
line 183: " `line`  - refers to the line number where the change starts
line 184: " `count` - refers to the number of lines the change covers

line 3:   " To keep vim's start-up fast, do not process the buffer when vim is starting.
line 4:   " Instead process it a short time later.  Normally we would rely on our
line 5:   " CursorHold autocommand to handle this but it turns out CursorHold is not
line 6:   " guaranteed to fire if the user has not typed anything yet; so set up a
line 7:   " timer instead.  The disadvantage is that if CursorHold does fire, the
line 8:   " plugin will do a round of unnecessary work; but since there will not have
